This pass modifies 'vectorizable' loops\\n10: // and generates target-independent LLVM-IR.\\n11: // The vectorizer uses the TargetTransformInfo analysis to estimate the costs\\n12: // of instructions in order to estimate the profitability of vectorization.\\n13: //\\n14: // The loop vectorizer combines consecutive loop iterations into a single\\n15: // 'wide' iteration. After this transformation the index is incremented\\n16: // by the SIMD vector width, and not by one.\\n17: //\\n18: // This pass has four parts:\\n19: // 1. The main loop pass that drives the different parts.\\n20: // 2. LoopVectorizationLegality - A unit that checks for the legality\\n21: //    of the vectorization.\\n22: // 3. InnerLoopVectorizer - A unit that performs the actual\\n23: //    widening of instructions.\\n24: // 4. LoopVectorizationCostModel - A unit that checks for the profitability\\n25: //    of vectorization. It decides on the optimal vector width, which\\n26: //    can be one, if vectorization is not profitable.\\n27: //\\n28: // There is a development effort going on to migrate loop vectorizer to the\\n29: // VPlan infrastructure and to introduce outer loop vectorization support (see\\n30: // docs/VectorizationPlan.rst and\\n31: // http://lists.llvm.org/pipermail/llvm-dev/2017-December/119523.html). For this\\n32: // purpose, we temporarily introduced the VPlan-native vectorization path: an\\n33: // alternative vectorization path that is natively implemented on top of the\\n34: // VPlan infrastructure. See EnableVPlanNativePath for enabling.\\n35: //\\n36: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\\n37: //\\n38: // The reduction-variable vectorization is based on the paper:\\n39: //  D. Nuzman and R. Henderson. Multi-platform Auto-vectorization.\\n40: //\\n41: // Variable uniformity checks are inspired by:\\n42: //  Karrenberg, R. and Hack, S. Auto-Vectorization of Interleaved\\n46: //  Data for SIMD\\n47: //\\n48: // Other ideas/concepts are from:\\n49: //  A. Zaks and D. Nuzman. This pass modifies 'vectorizable' loops\n10: // and generates target-independent LLVM-IR.\n11: // The vectorizer uses the TargetTransformInfo analysis to estimate the costs\n12: // of instructions in order to estimate the profitability of vectorization.\n13: //\n14: // The loop vectorizer combines consecutive loop iterations into a single\n15: // 'wide' iteration. After this transformation the index is incremented\n16: // by the SIMD vector width, and not by one.\n17: //\n18: // This pass has four parts:\n19: // 1. The main loop pass that drives the different parts.\n20: // 2. LoopVectorizationLegality - A unit that checks for the legality\n21: //    of the vectorization.\n22: // 3. InnerLoopVectorizer - A unit that performs the actual\n23: //    widening of instructions.\n24: // 4. LoopVectorizationCostModel - A unit that checks for the profitability\n25: //    of vectorization. It decides on the optimal vector width, which\n26: //    can be one, if vectorization is not profitable.\n27: //\n28: // There is a development effort going on to migrate loop vectorizer to the\n29: // VPlan infrastructure and to introduce outer loop vectorization support (see\n30: // docs/VectorizationPlan.rst and\n31: // http://lists.llvm.org/pipermail/llvm-dev/2017-December/119523.html). For this\n32: // purpose, we temporarily introduced the VPlan-native vectorization path: an\n33: // alternative vectorization path that is natively implemented on top of the\n34: // VPlan infrastructure. See EnableVPlanNativePath for enabling.\n35: //\n36: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n37: //\n38: // The reduction-variable vectorization is based on the paper:\n39: //  D. Nuzman and R. Henderson. Multi-platform Auto-vectorization.\n40: //\n41: // Variable uniformity checks are inspired by:\n42: //  Karrenberg, R. and Hack, S. Whole Function Vectorization.\n43: //\n44: // The interleaved access vectorization is based on the paper:\n45: //  Dorit Nuzman, Ira Rosen and Ayal Zaks.  Auto-Vectorization of Interleaved\n46: //  Data for SIMD\n47: //\n48: // Other ideas/concepts are from:\n49: //  A. Zaks and D. Nuzman. Autovectorization in GCC-two years later.\n50: //\n51: //  S. //===- LoopVectorize.cpp - A Loop Vectorizer ------------------------------===//\n2: //\n3: // Part of the LLVM Project, under the Apache License v2.0 with LLVM Exceptions.\n4: // See https://llvm.org/LICENSE.txt for license information.\n5: // SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0 WITH LLVM-exception\n6: //\n7: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n8: //\n9: // This is the LLVM loop vectorizer. This pass modifies 'vectorizable' loops\n10: // and generates target-independent LLVM-IR.\n11: // The vectorizer uses the TargetTransformInfo analysis to estimate the costs\n12: // of instructions in order to estimate the profitability of vectorization.\n13: //\n14: // The loop vectorizer combines consecutive loop iterations into a single\n15: // 'wide' iteration. After this transformation the index is incremented\n16: // by the SIMD vector width, and not by one.\n17: //\n18: // This pass has three parts:\n19: // 1. The main loop pass that drives the different parts.\n20: // 2. LoopVectorizationLegality - A unit that checks for the legality\n21: //    of the vectorization.\n22: // 3. InnerLoopVectorizer - A unit that performs the actual\n23: //    widening of instructions.\n24: // 4. LoopVectorizationCostModel - A unit that checks for the profitability\n25: //    of vectorization. It decides on the optimal vector width, which\n26: //    can be one, if vectorization is not profitable.\n27: //\n28: // There is a development effort going on to migrate loop vectorizer to the\n29: // VPlan infrastructure and to introduce outer loop vectorization support (see\n30: // docs/VectorizationPlan.rst and\n31: // http://lists.llvm.org/pipermail/llvm-dev/2017-December/119523.html). For this\n32: // purpose, we temporarily introduced the VPlan-native vectorization path: an\n33: // alternative vectorization path that is natively implemented on top of the\n34: // VPlan infrastructure. See EnableVPlanNativePath for enabling.\n35: //\n36: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n37: //\n38: // The reduction-variable vectorization is based on the paper:\n39: //  D. Nuzman and R. Henderson. Multi-platform Auto-vectorization.\n40: //\n41: // Variable uniformity checks are inspired by:\n42: //  Karrenberg, R. and Hack, S. Whole Function Vectorization.\n43: //\n44: // The interleaved access vectorization is based on the paper:\n45: //  Dorit Nuzman, Ira Rosen and Ayal Zaks.  Auto-Vectorization of Interleaved\n46: //  Data for SIMD\n47: //\n48: // Other ideas/concepts are from:\n49: //  A. Zaks and D. Nuzman. Autovectorization in GCC-two years later.\n50: //\n51: //  S. Maleki, Y. Gao, M. Garzaran, T. Wong and D. Padua.  An Evaluation of\n52: //  Vectorizing Compilers.\n53: //\n54: //===----------------------------------------------------------------------===//\n55: \n56: #include
